Lawyers Association Corrects the Abuse of Litigation Fees 129

The Shanghai Lawyers Association has submitted a document to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court to request the correction of the abuse of litigation fees. The original submission is excerpted below: The document is submitted for referral. According to a letter from member Huang Han, the Shanghai First Special District Local Court is abusing litigation fees. Please negotiate with the association. The matter should be handled by Mr. Xiang Zhang (full text omitted). After the association's staff reviewed the matter, they stated that "Revised Article 7 of the Rules on Litigation Fees stipulates that civil application fees are classified as trial fees. Therefore, various applications for trial should be paid. After the judgment is final, various applications for execution should not be charged again if the execution fee has already been paid. Member Huang's proposal is reasonable." The 198th joint meeting of the association's executive and supervisory committees resolved to forward the request to your court for correction. We hereby submit this document to request your court's review and implementation for the public benefit. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai First Special District Local Court, with the seals of the Standing Committee of the Shanghai Lawyers Association, Shen Junru, Chen Rui, and Wang Weizhen.

Chen Liqing and Son Accused of Abandonment by Daughter-in-Law, Case Withdrawn Due to Procedural Irregularities, Must First Report to Police 130

Chen Liqing, a wealthy hardware merchant from Guangdong with over two million in assets, and his son, Chen Guohua, were recently sued for criminal abandonment by Chen's daughter-in-law, Chen Tang Deyi (40 years old, resident of No. 91, Yongan Li, North Sichuan Road, Guohua's wife). She hired lawyer Xiong Fei and filed the lawsuit with the First Special District Court, requesting that they be punished according to Article 310 of the Criminal Law and demanding 84,600 yuan for living and medical expenses as a civil suit attachment. According to the suit, Tang Deyi came from a prominent family. At the age of 18, while studying in Shanghai, she was seen by Chen Guohua, who was captivated by her beauty. He immediately proposed to Tang's parents, vowing to die if the marriage did not succeed. Tang's family, out of pity, agreed to the marriage. However, Tang contracted an illness, so the marriage was postponed until 1916. After the marriage, Chen Guohua did not work and relied entirely on his father's support. Later, Tang's adoptive father, Mo Gansheng, returned from overseas and saw that Tang Deyi was suffering intolerable abuse from her in-laws. He bought her a house on Avenue Joffre and invested 40,000 taels to help Chen obtain a position as a compradore at the Han Yun Foreign Firm. From then on, Chen Guohua's life became increasingly affluent, and he indulged in pleasure, spending money like water, leading to mounting debts. Tang pawned her private jewelry for 2,000 yuan to repay the debts. However, Guohua, as a prodigal son, cohabitated with a woman surnamed Yu and a prostitute. He even raped his sister-in-law (Tang's younger sister), causing her to become pregnant. After giving birth, he abandoned her again. Tang gave birth to five children. During the January 28th Incident, Tang went to Hong Kong to mediate because her husband and adoptive father, Mo Gansheng, were in constant litigation. Chen placed the children with his sister in Hong Kong for Tang to raise. However, he did not provide any living expenses for the children. Tang was also seriously ill at this time, but he did not provide any medical expenses. In September, when she recovered from her illness and returned to Shanghai, she discovered that Chen Guohua was cohabitating with a tutor, Cai Huiying. Upon seeing Tang, he verbally abused her and moved all the furniture out of the house, never visiting Tang again. His father, Chen Liqing, although possessing over two million in assets, was also stingy with providing living expenses for his daughter-in-law. Therefore, she believed it was a clear case of joint abandonment by father and son and filed the lawsuit. The attached civil suit requested 72,000 yuan for Tang's monthly living expenses of 300 yuan for 20 years, plus 12,600 yuan for medical and other expenses. Judge Jiang Shuzi of the First Special District Court accepted the case. Based on Article 339 of the Criminal Procedure Law, spouses are not allowed to sue each other. Therefore, Tang Deyi was only summoned to the Criminal Court 8 yesterday afternoon and informed that spouses cannot sue each other. The procedure was thus deemed non-compliant. She should first report to the police for prosecution to be legitimate; otherwise, the case should be withdrawn to file a report to the police. If the case is not withdrawn and a report is filed with the police, the police will not accept it because a case cannot be pursued in two ways. Tang and her lawyer, upon hearing this, immediately expressed their willingness to withdraw the case and file a report with the police instead. Judge Jiang then declared the case inadmissible.

Pawned Warehouse Receipt Disowned Upon Maturity, Rong Zongjing Accused, Rong Failed to Appear Yesterday, Summons Re-scheduled 131

Flour magnate Rong Zongjing has been greatly affected by the recent economic downturn. His flour business has not been profitable, and his spinning mill has failed, leading to a mountain of debt and nearing bankruptcy, resulting in numerous lawsuits. In February of last year, Rong urgently needed funds, so he used a warehouse receipt from the Shenxin Third Spinning Mill in his hometown of Wuxi under the name of Fuxin Flour Company to mortgage for 60,000 yuan to the Xin Kang firm in this city, signing a mortgage agreement. When the term expired, Rong had no funds to repay the loan. Therefore, the creditor, according to the agreed terms, sent a letter to the Shenxin Third Mill in Wuxi, instructing them to deliver the 400 bales of cotton yarn listed on the pawned warehouse receipt as collateral. Unexpectedly, the mill replied to Xin Kang, denying that the goods were mortgaged, stating that "Our mill has no dealings with your firm, and this mortgage cannot be recognized. Please contact the original handler." However, Xin Kang believes that the mortgage agreement was personally signed by Rong Zongjing and that he is now trying to deny it, which constitutes intentional fraud. Sun Bosheng, representing Xin Kang, has filed a criminal self-accusation against Rong Zongjing for fraud and obtaining property. Yesterday afternoon, a judge from the First Special District Local Court held a hearing at Xiang Yinghua. The defendant, Rong Zongjing, failed to appear. Sun Bosheng recounted the mortgage process and presented the mortgage agreement and warehouse receipt. He further clarified the effect of the warehouse receipt, stating that in the market, warehouse receipts for goods are considered equivalent to the actual goods. If the warehouse receipt cannot be used to collect the goods, it is no different from a blank check. In other words, a warehouse receipt is the actual goods. Although the warehouse receipt mortgaged by the defendant is valid, because the mill denied the mortgage, it was impossible to collect the goods. However, the defendant is the general manager of Fuxin and Shenxin mills. Since he used the mill's warehouse receipt to borrow funds and failed to repay it upon maturity, he should allow the goods to be collected. His refusal to deliver the goods constitutes fraud and obtaining property. The court stated that the case involves fraud and that the defendant should appear in court to provide evidence. The hearing was adjourned to the afternoon of the 18th of this month, and Rong Zongjing was summoned to court for further questioning.

Today's Grand Opening of the Takahama Seaside Resort, Greatly Renovated and Brand New 132

The Takahama Seaside Resort, since being taken over by the city this year and entrusted to the Xingye Reliance Society, has been greatly renovated and is brand new. Details have been reported in previous newspapers. It is now known that the resort is scheduled to open today. Details are listed below:

Various Features (1) The sand on the beach of the Takahama Seaside Resort was originally a kind of bright, clean, and fine sand, lovely and delightful. However, it was mixed with stones and uneven. This year, the stones have been removed and sifted, and fine sand has been added, making it soft and comfortable. (2) The tides of the sea are signaled by bells and flags. Markers are also erected in deep-water areas to ensure safety. (3) New pools, water towers, and showers have been built, and hot and cold-water faucets have been installed for bathing. (4) There are thousands of mu of open space in the resort, which can be used to build temporary summer villas, saving Shanghainese people the trouble of traveling to other cities. (5) A lake has been specially opened in the resort, with a pavilion built in the center of the lake, bounded by a long dike, bridged by wooden bridges, and with vast, shaded walkways. Over four thousand trees have been planted, and over five hundred square feet of lawn has been laid, with flourishing flowers and trees and green grass like a carpet.

Water and Land Transportation The City Ferry has built a new No. 6 ferry this year. The speed and decoration are superior to those of the No. 5 ferry. The front deck is also equipped with copper windows that can be opened and closed at any time depending on the weather. It will join the Shanghai-Songjiang line on the first of next month and operate to Takahama, providing extra comfort for tourists. As for land transportation, the road from Takahama Wharf to the seaside has been widened by the Bureau of Public Works. In addition to the original six buses, four new buses have recently been added to the route, making it smooth and comfortable. Compared to previous years, it is like heaven and earth.

Dining Facilities The resort has a large-scale dining hall that can accommodate 400 people for meals. It is covered with emerald green Spanish-style roof tiles and surrounded by steel windows, making it extremely bright. Looking far away, the water and sky merge into one, and the scenery is excellent. The various foods are generally handled by the City Ferry, with French-style Western food and Yangzhou snacks, which are clean, tasty, and reasonably priced.

Grand Opening Today The seaside resort was completed last week, and Chinese and foreign tourists have been flocking to it ever since. It officially opens this morning without any ceremonies. It is also scheduled to invite people from all walks of life and newspaper reporters to visit at the beginning of next month.

The Chinese Red Cross Society Second Hospital to Cease Operations 133

Outpatient Services Cease on the 20th, Expediting Closure, Inpatients Transferred to Other Hospitals, Employee Salaries Paid Until the End of June

The Chinese Red Cross Society Second Hospital, located at No. 856 Xinzha Road, ceased operations on the 20th of this month (the day before yesterday). The hospital is currently expediting its closure in order to hand over the premises. Inpatients have also been transferred to other hospitals. Employee salaries were paid yesterday. The Datong News Agency reporter has gathered the following details:

Brief History of the Hospital The hospitals established by the Shanghai General Headquarters of the Chinese Red Cross Society are divided into the First Hospital, the Second Hospital, and the Third Hospital. The First Hospital is located at No. 363 Haig Road and is headed by Mr. Yan Fuqing. The Third Hospital is located at the Dada Wharf on the Outer Bund in Nanshi and is headed by Mr. Wang Yiting. The hospital that is ceasing operations is the Second Hospital, located at No. 856 Xinzha Road, which is headed by Mr. Wang Peiyuan. The vice-director and medical director is Mr. Xu Zhaorong.

Medical Facilities The Second Branch has been established for over 20 years. The original location was on Tianjin Road, then Beijing Road, and finally moved to Xinzha Road. The hospital is relatively large in scale, and the medical facilities are extremely complete. It has eight wards with first, second, and third class rooms, with a total of 61 beds. There are eight physicians, including the medical director, 33 nurses and staff, and 18 servants, totaling 48 people.

Reasons for Closure The General Headquarters is now saving expenses and implementing austerity measures. After deliberation by the board of directors, it was decided to close the hospital. The upper level of the hospital will be used as the General Headquarters' office, and the lower level will still operate an outpatient department in the future. After the board of directors made the decision, the hospital was notified and ordered to begin closing on the 20th of this month. Employee salaries were also paid in full by the General Headquarters yesterday afternoon, up to the end of June.

Disposition of Patients As of the 20th of this month, there were still 35 patients in the hospital. In the afternoon, the General Headquarters sent staff to properly transfer one person to the First Hospital on Haig Road, seven people to the Third Hospital on the Outer Bund in Nanshi, and nine people to the Shanghai Epidemic Hospital on Xizang Road. The remaining 18 people were taken back by the Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Society and transferred to other hospitals on their own.

Handling of Closure Most of the hospital's physicians, nurses, staff, and servants have remained at the hospital and are currently handling the closure in preparation for the handover. Food is also being maintained by the General Hospital as usual for the time being. However, according to the hospital's staff, they have served at the hospital for many years. Now that it is closed, they hope that the General Headquarters can provide some severance pay to help them return to their hometowns.

Notice of Ceasing Outpatient Services The hospital's notice of ceasing outpatient services is excerpted below: We hereby inform you that this hospital has received a letter from the General Headquarters of the Chinese Red Cross Society stating that the first board of directors meeting has resolved to close the Second Hospital immediately and move the General Headquarters' office in, etc. In accordance with this order, outpatient services will be suspended from the 20th of this month, and no new inpatients will be admitted in order to complete the closure. This notice is hereby issued for general information. Chinese Red Cross Society Second Hospital.

The Kidnapping of Li Guanlin's Young Son: Thirty Kidnappers Arrested, Second Special Court Interrogates Suspects Yesterday, Mastermind of Kidnapping is Li Guanlin's Brother-in-Law 134

—Those Deemed Unrelated to the Case Will Be Sent Back to the Place Where the Crime Occurred for Handling—

Li Guanlin, a local villager residing at the Li family residence on the western end of Route Tenant de la Tour in the French Concession, is thirty-six years old and makes a living as a farmer. Over the years, he has diligently cultivated the land and acquired several acres of property. His wife, Mrs. Wang, is thirty-eight years old and has given birth to four daughters and one son. The youngest son, named Jinxiang, is three years old. His elderly mother used to treat children for fright-related illnesses, and Li has accumulated considerable wealth. However, his timid nature has attracted the attention of bandits. On the evening of the thirteenth of last month, around 7:00 PM, while Li's wife was returning home and was sitting with his mother and children around the stove having dinner, three kidnappers suddenly arrived, all dressed in black. They knocked on the door, claiming to be requesting the old lady to see a sick child. Li's third daughter, unaware of the deception, opened the door and let them in. One of the bandits immediately monitored Li's movements, brandishing a pistol and threatening him not to panic. Another monitored everyone in the house, while the third snatched Li's son, Jinxiang, from his wife Wang's arms, covering the child's mouth to prevent him from crying out. They then rushed out the door and fled. As they left, the bandits fired a warning shot into the air and ran away. Li and his family were stunned and dared not resist or raise an alarm. They watched the kidnappers disappear into the distance before reporting the incident to the French police station on Avenue Petain, requesting an investigation. Subsequently, Li received repeated letters from the kidnappers demanding a ransom of 100,000 yuan for the child's release, which was later reduced to 50,000 yuan. Despite Li entrusting someone to negotiate with the kidnappers five times, an agreement could not be reached due to the significant difference in the amounts. The day before yesterday, Li received another letter from the kidnappers, asking Li to be in Zhabei between 11:00 AM and 1:00 PM on the 20th, and specified that the representative must be bald, wear a long black cloth gown, hold a newspaper in one hand and a sugarcane in the other as a sign. They also specified the route: going north from Xinza Bridge on Datong Road, turning right onto Xinmin Road, crossing the dry bridge, heading north on Minde Road, east on Hongjiang Road, Huwen Road, to Zhonghua Xin Road, where someone would come to negotiate. Upon receiving the letter, Li entrusted his brother-in-law, Chen Er'a (aka Chen Yongxiang, 35 years old, residing at No. 11 Tangjiabang, Pudong, a tailor who runs a tailoring stall, Li's younger sister, named Xiannan, was lured away by Chen six years ago on the seventh day of the seventh lunar month and later became his wife), to act as his representative. Following the instructions, Chen went on time to negotiate with the kidnappers. This matter was detected by Inspector Jin Jiulin of the French police, who, at 9:00 AM the day before yesterday, led interpreters Li Xianyang, detectives Zhou Buguang, Zhang Ziying, Deputy Detectives Qin Youyu, Detectives Zhong Benchang, Dai Rongji, Wu Wengang, Yang Jiaxue, and others to the Zhabei Fourth District Public Security Bureau, requesting police detectives to disguise themselves and lie in ambush near the dry bridge on Xinmin Road. Soon, a man wearing a white cloth short gown and black cloth trousers (i.e., the kidnapper Zhao Taotao), holding an umbrella, was seen standing in front of No. 510 Xinmin Road, waiting for two hours. At noon, when the principal's representative, Chen Er'a, passed by, he did not speak to the kidnapper and went straight ahead. After a while, two men were seen passing by the dry bridge on Xinmin Road, talking to the man with the umbrella, asking about how Chen Er'a was approaching the matter. The detectives, who were disguised and waiting nearby, overheard these words and were certain that the three were kidnappers. They immediately arrested the three and took them to the Public Security Bureau. Under interrogation, they confessed their names: Zhao Taotao (26 years old, from Zhenjiang, lives at No. 10, Lane 191, Jialan Road, unemployed), Dong Aqing (31 years old, from Nantong, lives at No. 5, Ranggui Lane, Haining Road, works as a cook), and Chen Jinsheng (aka Zhou Yunda, 31 years old, from Nantong, lives in a bungalow at No. 238, Lane Awenyi Road, Parker Road, works as a rickshaw puller). According to Zhao's confession, the kidnapping was masterminded and planned by the principal's brother-in-law, Chen Er'a, to demand a ransom. Yao Shaobai, who lives at No. 2 Zichai Xia Road, and Fang Dairang, who lives at No. 714 Yangshupu Road, must be detained before the matter can be resolved. The detectives then took Yao, Dong, and Chen back to the police station. Meanwhile, they went to the principal's house to arrest the main suspect, Chen Er'a. They also went to No. 2 Zixia Road and arrested Yang Shaobai (aka Yang Shanchang, 40 years old, from Haimen), Gu Linshi (30 years old, from Songjiang, lives at No. 79 Langjia Bridge, Nanshi, works in iron carriage tailoring), Ji Xiucheng (33 years old, from Chongming, lives at No. 56 Xiexing Lane, Haichao Road, Nanshi, a vendor). They also went to No. 714 Yangshupu Road and arrested Fang Dairang (46 years old, from Chongming, a worker) and Fang's mistress, Chen Zhu (40 years old, from Chongming), Xu Longtou (32 years old, from Shanghai, lives at No. 10, Lane 191, Lan Road), Lu Zhihai (20 years old, from Yangzhou, lives with Xu Longtou). They then went to Room 1 of the Fuxing Hotel at No. 717 Beile Road and arrested suspects Hu Youhua (46 years old, from Haimen, lives in Yejia Lane, Dananmen, owner of Changchun Teahouse), Xu Weimin (aka Li Huiming, 30 years old, from Haiyan, Zhejiang, works in advertising, residing at No. 851 Beile Road), Wang Jinxiang (aka Wang Wei, 33 years old, from Ningbo, lives at No. 9 Yejia Lane, Dananmen), Zhang Shenggen (27 years old, from Qidong), Zhang Xiaogen (29 years old, from Haimen, lives at No. 84 Gongyi Lane, Yangshupu Road), Du Jinqing (49 years old, from Shanghai, lives at No. 10 Du Family Residence, Caojiadu North), Chen Caiqing (13 years old, from Haimen, lives at No. 21 Lan Road, Yangshupu Road), Wang He (30 years old, from Nantong, lives at No. 51 Lan Road, Yangshupu Road), Shi Lao'er (43 years old, from Haimen, lives at No. 53 Deyuan Lane, Shenjia Beach, Yangshupu Road), Chen Liangshi (46 years old, from Haimen, lives at No. 8 Tangjiabang, Yinxiang Port), Zhu Xiaobao (26 years old, from Qidong), Zhang Yuanliang (34 years old, from Haimen), Shen Yucheng (27 years old, from Qidong, lives in a bungalow on Mayushan Road), and thirteen others. Finally, based on the guidance of the arrested Fang Dairang, they went to a thatched hut in the fields of Jiangxinsha, Pudong, and retrieved the kidnapped child, arresting the guards Su Zhaogen (32 years old, from Chongming, the owner of the house where the child was hidden), Yang Hongde (43 years old, from Nantong), Shi Nianqing (29 years old, from Haimen), Huang Jiuchu (from Chongming), Wu Zufang (30 years old, from Haimen), and Chen Meifang (female, 22 years old, from Haimen), totaling thirty men and women arrested. Except for Shi Nianqing, Huang Jiuchu, Wu Zufang, and Chen Meifang, who were detained at the Public Security Bureau pending a formal request for their transfer, the remaining suspects, along with the kidnapped child, were taken back to the police station. The kidnapped child was escorted home, and the suspects were placed in separate cells. After investigation, it was found that Zhao Taotao had committed a crime endangering the Republic of China in 1930, for which he was sentenced to seven years in prison by the First Special Court, later reduced to five years after appeal. Dong Aqing committed a kidnapping in the Public Concession in 1930 and was sentenced to six years by the First Special Court. Chen Jinsheng committed extortion in the French Concession in 1929 and was sentenced to two years. Hu Youhua, Xu Weimin, Wang Jinxiang, and others had also committed crimes in the past. Yesterday, the police sent Zhao and the other twenty-six suspects to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District Local Court. Judge Zhang Chaozuo, accompanied by clerk Gao Yan, presided over the trial. After questioning the suspects about their age, residence, and address, Gu Shouxi, a lawyer from the police department, outlined the case, stating that the defendants had been arrested for kidnapping and extortion, and the number of people arrested was very large. He requested a longer period for the police to conduct a detailed investigation and then file a suit for trial, asking that the defendants be temporarily detained. Detective Zhou Buguang then reported on the arrest process, stating that after arresting Yao, Dong, and Chen, Yao confessed that the kidnapping was instigated by the plaintiff Li Guanlin's brother-in-law, Chen Er'a, aka Chen Yongxiang. Chen was then arrested. It was later found that Chen had eloped with the plaintiff's sister and had not been in contact with them. However, on May 13, after the plaintiff's son was kidnapped, Chen Er'a came to the plaintiff's house on the 15th to inquire about the news, offering to help search for the child, and taking 250 yuan from the plaintiff. He also hired Yang, a lawyer from Baker Road, to write to the police station, requesting the withdrawal of the detectives stationed in the plaintiff's house. Because the police refused, this clue was obtained, leading to the solving of the case. At this point, the court ordered the defendants to be taken down and questioned separately. Yao Taotao was first questioned and initially denied involvement. After repeated questioning, he claimed that on May 5 or 6, a man named Su and Fang Dairang said that there was a man named Chen who had a son with each of his wives and was fighting over property. The first wife wanted to kill the second wife's son and asked to borrow a house to temporarily hide the child. He overheard this conversation. Now that he had been arrested, Detective Chang asked him about the child's whereabouts, and he replied with what Su and Fang had said before. Later, the detectives took him to Fang Dairang's place, and together with Fang, they retrieved the child, who they said was the child in question. However, he did not know who had kidnapped the child. He had returned to Zhenjiang because his wife had died and had only arrived in Shanghai yesterday after receiving a letter from a man named Wang who had helped him find work. Dong Aqing and Chen Jinsheng were then brought in for questioning, but they both denied participating in the kidnapping, claiming that they had only confessed under torture at the Public Security Bureau. Chen Er'a claimed that he was not the mastermind behind the kidnapping and that the child was his nephew, so how could he do such a thing? At this point, Detective Zhou Buguang stated to the court that Yang Hongde, who was guarding the child, had been sent by Chen Er'a and had now been arrested. He requested that Chen be confronted with this evidence. However, Chen still stubbornly denied the accusation, answering questions evasively. Su Zhaogen claimed that he farmed in Jiangxinsha and that Fang Dairang and a large woman had brought the child to him, saying that the child was being temporarily hidden for ten days or so due to a lawsuit between the first and second wives, and that he knew nothing about the kidnapping. Yang Hongde claimed that Chen Er'a had asked him to take care of the child. On the seventeenth day of the fourth lunar month, a man named Sha A'er introduced him to Chen Er'a at a small teahouse near Yangshupu Bridge. Chen Er'a told him that the first and second wives were fighting a lawsuit and that the first wife wanted to kill the second wife's son, asking him to take care of the child, promising to pay him half a yuan per day and provide him with food. He did not know Chen Er'a before. The court ordered Chen Er'a to be confronted with Yang Hongde, but Chen continued to deny everything, claiming that someone was trying to frame him. Fang Dairang claimed that Su Zhaogen was his friend and that a man named Sha and a female barber had come to him saying that the first wife wanted to kill the second wife's son due to a lawsuit between the first and second wives, asking him to borrow a house in the countryside to temporarily hide the child, far away so that it would not be found. He agreed, and a woman named Chen brought the child to him, claiming to be the second wife. On May 18, he handed the child over to Su, not knowing anything about the kidnapping. The court then questioned each of the other suspects one by one, but they all claimed to be unrelated to the case. The court reviewed the evidence and decided to postpone the trial to July 6. The defendants were remanded in custody. The court also instructed the police to release any defendants who were found to be unrelated to the case to avoid detaining innocent people. The court adjourned.

The Secret Drug Manufacturing Operation Inside Fengchang Rice Store: Wang Baosheng Sentenced to Five Years and Fined One Thousand Yuan, Cao Qi and Others Also Sentenced, Drugs Confiscated 135

A secret drug manufacturing operation was discovered inside the Fengchang Rice Store on Tiantong Road, producing morphine and other potent drugs. Taking advantage of the opportunity to transport rice, the drugs were placed in hemp bags and delivered to various buyers. This secret operation was originally difficult to expose. However, after a long period of time, the Xinza Police Station became aware of it and sent detectives to conduct a thorough investigation. Finally, on the morning of the 28th of last month, they intercepted a drug delivery suspect on Xizang Road and immediately went to search the rice store. They seized potent drugs and manufacturing equipment on the spot, and successively arrested the suspects Wang Baosheng and thirteen others, handing them over to the First Special District Local Court for investigation. The details have been previously reported. The investigating detectives escorted all the suspects to the court, and the police lawyer Qian Xunjiu also appeared in court. Sheng Yuchang is Accused of Abandonment, Appeal Heard, Lin Yujin Dissatisfied with Sheng's Suspended Sentence, Sheng Also Appealed, Demanding Dismissal 136

—The Plaintiff Believes the Appellant's Evidence is Suspicious—

Sheng Yuchang, 39, grandson of Sheng Xuanhuai, former Minister of Posts and Communications and Railway Minister of the Qing Dynasty, residing in a Western-style house at No. 1, Avenue Petain, French Concession, was previously sued by his concubine, Lin Yujin, a Guangdong woman (28), through a lawyer in the Criminal Court of the Second Special Court for abandonment. The trial resulted in Sheng being sentenced to six months in prison, suspended for one year. Sheng was dissatisfied with the judgment and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The plaintiff, Lin Yujin, was also dissatisfied with Sheng's suspended sentence and simultaneously filed an appeal, requesting the suspension be revoked and the sentence carried out. The details have been reported in this newspaper. The case has been approved by the High Court. Yesterday morning, Presiding Judge Guo Dechang, together with Judges Fan Peien and Wang Cheng, and Prosecutor Zhang Zongru, specially convened the Third Criminal Court to hear the case. Lin Yujin was represented by her agents, Hua Maosheng, Huang Zengjie, and Zhu Zhengshan, due to illness. The appellant Sheng Yuchang, accompanied by his defense lawyer, appeared in court. First, the lawyers representing the appellant Lin Yujin stated that Lin Yujin was suffering from severe heart and lung diseases and was currently being treated in the hospital, so she could not appear in court. Lin had previously married the defendant as a concubine, but was later forced to leave. Lin then worked as a dancer in Shanghai. After the January 28th Incident, the defendant met Lin at a dance hall, and they rekindled their old feelings. They then rented the front building at No. 291 Renheli, Avenue Joffre, and lived together, promising to move back to the main residence. Later, the defendant suddenly stopped visiting due to Lin Yujin's lung disease. This situation constituted abandonment. The initial judgment of a suspended sentence was inappropriate, so she filed an appeal, requesting a change in the judgment. Sheng Yuchang testified that he married Lin Yujin, a Guangdong singer, as a concubine in January 1924. Later, she voluntarily and unconditionally left him. The judge asked if they had met again at a dance hall in Shanghai, and he replied no. He had stayed at home during the January 28th Incident and had not gone out. The judge asked if there had been any relationship afterward, and he replied no. At this point, his representative lawyer stated that they had found a telephone directory listing Huang Tiyu, the owner of a shoe repair shop at No. 291 Avenue Joffre, who could prove that Sheng Yuchang had never visited Lin Yujin. This would prove that Lin had been living with another lover. Huang was present and could be summoned for questioning. The judge ordered Huang to be brought before the court. Huang testified that he had rented the storefront at No. 291 Avenue Joffre in February 1932 and opened a shoe repair shop. Lin Yujin and her husband, surnamed Tan, lived upstairs. Tan was present and listening to the trial. The judge ordered him to be identified. Huang turned his head and pointed to the person sitting in the second row at the end of the audience, answering that it was him. The judge ordered the bailiff to bring Tan before the court. Tan testified that his name was Tan Fumin, and he lived on the third floor of No. 291 Avenue Joffre and had no cohabiting relationship with Lin Yujin. The judge then ordered the lawyers from both sides to begin their arguments. First, Lin's representative lawyer argued that the initial judgment of six months imprisonment, suspended, was because the defendant had never received a criminal sentence. However, this was not the case. Sheng Yuchang had previously been involved in litigation through lawyers over his concubines, and there was a record. The defendant himself claimed to have four or five concubines, showing that he relied on wealth and power, treating women as playthings. This behavior should be severely punished. As for the witness the defendant invited today, there was clear collusion. If the defendant had never been to No. 291 Avenue Joffre, how could he know there was a shoe repair shop? If he knew about the shoe repair shop, how could he know the owner's name? Telephone directories only list the shop name. Not only was Huang Tiyu present to testify, but Tan was also identified as Lin's lover. This matter was clearly collusive and should be investigated. Sheng's defense lawyer then presented evidence and argued at length, stating that the defendant had not resumed cohabitation with Lin and requested that the original judgment be revoked and he be declared not guilty. By noon, the court declared the arguments concluded and scheduled the verdict for 2:00 PM on the 28th.

Municipal Radio Station to Begin Broadcasting by End of Next Month, Equipment Room Completed, Actively Installing Equipment, Unique in Shanghai, 150 Radios to be Installed 137

The municipal radio station being established by the Shanghai Municipal Government, which has been designed by the Municipal Public Works Bureau, has been in the works for several months. According to reports, the equipment room has been completed, and equipment is being actively installed. It is determined that broadcasting will begin before the 30th of next month. The details are as follows:

Equipment Room Completed: After the Municipal Public Works Bureau took charge, it entrusted the construction of the radio station's equipment room, antenna base, and sheet piles to the Zhulunji Construction Company. The equipment room has now been completed. It is located behind the municipal government building and is divided into three rooms: a communications room, an equipment room, and a mechanic's room. Two antennas, each 120 feet high, have been erected. Other wire pipes are approximately 1,000 feet long and are still being actively installed. It is reported that the total value of the station's equipment is approximately 30,000 yuan.

Scheduled Broadcasting: The antennas and other equipment are expected to be installed soon. The municipal government has set a target date of broadcasting by the 30th of next month. It is reported that the station's frequency is 900 RC and its power is 500 watts, making it one of the largest in the area. The original plan was for 40 radios, but this has been increased to 150, which will be installed in busy areas in various districts. The types of broadcasts will mainly consist of lectures, current affairs, and education, with occasional performances of high-class music.

Two Children Caught Transporting Drugs 138

Over Four Thousand Red Pills Found, Two More Suspects Arrested and Sent to the Bureau for Handling

Yang Ziqing, residing at No. 1 Shiping Lane, Zhuhang Lane, Nanshi, is unemployed and makes a living by selling red pill drugs. Recently, Yang used children from neighboring families and relatives to carry red pills to various ports, from where they were taken to various parts of the interior for sale, generating considerable profits. At around 5:00 PM the night before last, Yang again sent his nephew, a boy named Ma Xiaolin from Haimen, and a girl named Song Xiulang from Chongming, residing at No. 124 Shengyi Lane, Shengyi Wharf, Nanshi, to transport red pills hidden on their bodies to the Hongda steamer at Pier 9 (Datong Wharf), intending to hand them over. However, their plan was discovered by Dong Mingde, captain of the Sixteenth Bund Detective Squad of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, who sent detectives Zhang Zhongliang, Yuan Mingcai, Fu Sanbao, and Li Fatong to the vicinity of Pier 9 (Datong Wharf). They noticed two children, a boy and a girl, around ten years old, looking nervous and suspicious, and decided to check them. They found five packs of red pills, each containing five hundred pills, totaling two thousand five hundred pills, hidden on the boy's body. They also found two thousand red pills in a pocket bag around the girl's waist. The two children and the four thousand five hundred red pills were taken back to the squad for questioning. The boy confessed that his name was Ma Xiaolin, 14 years old, from Haimen, who came to Shanghai last year and resided with his maternal grandmother's family on Dapu Road. He currently lived with his maternal uncle Yang Ziqing at No. 1 Shiping Lane, Zhuhang Wharf, Nanshi. The red pills had been given to him yesterday by his maternal uncle at Yang's house, instructing him (Ma himself claimed) to bring them to the Hongda steamer at Datong Wharf this afternoon to be received by his maternal uncle Yang Ziqing. The girl confessed that her name was Song Xiulang, from Chongming, 11 years old, residing at No. 124 Shengyi Lane, Yisheng Wharf, Nanshi. Yang Ziqing had instructed her to hide four packs of red pills in her pocket bag, wrap it around her waist, and wear a floral cloth cheongsam over it to transport them to the Hongda steamer at Datong Wharf, promising to pay her one yuan as a reward, which had not yet been paid. She had delivered them once six or seven days ago, and Yang had given her one yuan to give to her mother. Yang, being well-informed, had already fled upon hearing the news. Only Yang's wife, Jiang, was arrested. In the front厢房, a package of red pills totaling five hundred pills was found in the bottom of the interlayer of a round 洋 iron box. The members of the unit then went to No. 124 Yisheng Lane and arrested Song Lushi (64 years old), a related person. In total, there were four people. After the Huang Branch Chief transmitted the case for interrogation, it was sent to the General Bureau for legal action this afternoon.

Recent Developments in the Meifeng Liquidation 140

Difficulty in Collecting Debts, According to the North-China Daily News, Mr. He Fu, the liquidator of Meifeng Bank, stated to a news reporter yesterday that the loans and overdrafts of Meifeng Bank totaled approximately 7 million yuan, of which only about 1.5% has been recovered to date. The lack of understanding of the liquidator by the debtors is regrettable. Since taking office as liquidator, he has repeatedly urged the repayment of debts by letters and telephone calls. Some people have responded, saying that they have no cash available but would pay a certain amount first, with the remainder to be paid in one week, one month, or even longer. This kind of behavior is commendable. However, the majority of people have simply ignored the calls, neither responding by letter nor sending someone to discuss the matter, and not even making a telephone call. Therefore, it is planned to resort to legal action from the beginning of next week to collect the debts as soon as possible. If the matter is delayed for a long time, even the salaries of the employees may not be fully paid. Currently, the company employs 35 people to handle the liquidation work, which is heavy, and the salaries are very low. It is difficult to predict when the liquidation will be completed. Someone called to ask if the money they had deposited in the bank could be recovered, or when they could withdraw it. He was told that it was not possible at the moment, and it was doubtful whether it would be possible in eight months. Even then, he could not guarantee that the full amount could be recovered. In the two weeks from the bank's closure to June 18, a total of 89,782.8 yuan was received. Including the cash stored on the day of the closure, 13,527.7 yuan, the total cash on hand is now 103,309.5 yuan. At that time, there was a total of 17,541.19 yuan in cash on the books, including 4,000 yuan in Meifeng Bank notes, which had long become worthless paper but was still stored in the vault and recorded as cash. This amount must be deducted. The amount owed to the Meidong 銀 Company is 178,749.5 yuan, of which only 4,186.92 yuan has been recovered in two weeks. The position of the Puyi 銀 Company is even worse. The amount owed is 216,902.82 yuan, of which only 2,000 yuan has been recovered in two weeks.

The Southern Goods Industry Association held a meeting of the executive and supervisory committees at Chongyi Hall yesterday. A quorum of committee members was present. Shen Yiqiu, the temporary chairman, reported on the election of the chairman and discussed and resolved several important cases. Yu, a representative from the Municipal Party Headquarters, and Yuan Hongjun, a representative from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, were present to supervise. The resolutions are recorded below: (1) Case of Ji Jinzhang's letter resigning from the position of chairman: Resolved, resignation approved. (2) The chairman of the association shall be re-elected by secret ballot in accordance with the association's constitution: Resolved, the election shall be conducted by the five standing committee members. The results of the ballot were as follows: Xu Bokang received votes, Liu Yunzhang received one vote, and one vote was invalid. Xu Bokang was elected as the successor chairman and reported to higher authorities for record. (3) Case of the industry being ordered to establish literacy schools: Resolved, approved as planned. (5) Case of whether the association's tea boy should be reduced: Resolved, to save expenses, only one is allowed. (6) Case of how to collect membership fees since the tea certificates of the industry have been recovered by the municipal market: Resolved, Long, Cheng, Xu, and Ni were jointly nominated to negotiate with the municipal market, and the membership fees are postponed. (8) Case of the association's evaluation committee's guarantee deposit checks collected last year being returned at the end of the year as resolved by the general meeting: Resolved, the checks shall be returned after the fines decided last year have been paid. The deadline for the checks is the end of July. The rent owed to the market shall be advanced by the committee members, with each contributing 500 yuan, to be paid within three days. The meeting was adjourned after the discussions.

Central Bank Inspection Report 147

The Central Bank's 236th Reserve Inspection Report states: This office is responsible for inspecting the reserve funds for the banknotes issued by this bank in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations. The 236th inspection was held at the Issuing Bureau of this bank on June 20, 1935. The results of the inspection are hereby announced as follows: (A) Total amount of banknotes issued in silver dollars: 10,123,9420 yuan, including 9,436,6578 yuan in silver dollar notes and 6,872,842 yuan in subsidiary coin notes. Total amount of reserve funds for banknotes: 10,123,9420 yuan, including 7,923,9420 yuan in cash reserves. The cash reserves consist of 7,515,9423 yuan stored in this bank's issuing treasury, 2,277,723 yuan stored in branch banks in various ports, and 1,802,274 yuan deposited with other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 2,200,000 yuan in silver dollars. (B) Total amount of Customs Gold Unit banknotes issued: 373,324.70 yuan. Total amount of reserve funds for Customs Gold Unit banknotes: 373,324.70 yuan. This reserve consists of 7,351.95 taels of standard gold, which, at a fixed price of 50779, is equivalent to 373,324.70 yuan in Customs Gold Units. In accordance with Article 2 of the Central Bank's Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guarantee reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is consistent with the regulations. This report is hereby issued. June 21, 1935. Li, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, Xie Mingxun, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jili.

Letter 153

Dear Sir, I read in your newspaper yesterday the first item of the basic meeting discussion of the Sugar, North and South Sundries Association, that Zheng Tongyong beat Zhang Zuwang in violation of market rules, and the market decided to fine him 25 yuan and a pair of candles, and ordered Zheng Tongyuan to come to the market within three days to comply. I was very surprised to read this. Tongyuan attended the executive and supervisory meeting of the Southern Goods Association on the 28th of last month. Zhang Zuwang suddenly broke into the market and wandered for a long time, and arbitrarily shouted in his mouth, which caused opposition from the crowd. After persuading him to withdraw, he became angry and reported to the Sugar Industry Association and fabricated a fake injury report, deceptively suing the local court. The court session was held on the 18th of this month, and the forensic doctor proved in court that there were no scars. The verdict is now scheduled to be announced on the 24th of this month. The Sugar, North and South Sundries Market believed in one-sided remarks, did not investigate the facts, and illegally punished Tongyuan, which Tongyuan finds difficult to accept. In addition to submitting a request to the Party and government authorities for thorough investigation, I am deeply afraid that the outside world will not understand the truth and cause misunderstandings. I hereby write to correct this. To the editor of Shenbao Newspaper, Zheng Tongyuan respectfully. June 21, 1935.

Dear Sir, I read in your newspaper on June 18 a news item about a young woman throwing herself into the river from a ferry, which stated that before the deceased woman threw herself into the river from the Taikoo Company's Quick and Large No. 1 launch, she handed a paper bag to another man, who reported to the water police station that his name was Wang Liansheng and that he was a waiter at the Zhongnan Hotel in this city. However, there is absolutely no such person as Wang Liansheng in our shop's waiters. It turns out that Wang Liansheng was a servant of a Mr. Shen who opened a long-term room in our shop last year, and has nothing to do with our shop. I don't know why he pretended to be a waiter in our shop. I hope your newspaper will correct this to clarify the facts and avoid misunderstandings. Zhongnan Hotel respectfully. June 21.

Spring and Autumn

Anecdotes 155

— (Sun Jianping)

Buzzing mosquitoes, everyone hates them! But there are some people who rely on them to live, and maybe even make some money from them. If you don't believe me? Then look at the many factories on the market that manufacture and sell large quantities of mosquito incense sticks. Isn't this a powerful piece of evidence!

The sun's heat is increasing the degrees on the thermometer day by day! The city girls are reducing the clothes on their bodies day by day, wearing only thin cicada-wing gauze shirts, and strolling leisurely on the streets with their bare white legs, but if you look closely, there seem to be faint frostbite scars! But the girls in the countryside are also baring their legs, because they have been tanned by the sun, and you can't even see if there are any frostbite scars! They are working hard in the fields.

Calligrapher Mei Tiaoding 156

— Country Old Man

In the early years of the Guangxu reign in the Qing Dynasty, in the era when scholars were obsessed with the imperial examinations, those scholars who were repeatedly unsuccessful in the thorny examinations often set up schools to teach and make a living by training children. Among them, there were many talented people who were buried in poor alleys and small houses, forming poetry societies and studying ancient texts to pass the boring years. There were also many people who used calligraphy and painting to relieve their boredom.

Mr. Mei Youzhu Tiaoding of our county was of noble character and his calligraphy was famous throughout the country. He was poor and made a living by setting up schools. There were no servants at home. When a friend came to his house, the wooden door was closed and self-opened. He often saw Mr. Dao Mao standing proudly, hanging his wrist to write couplets, and his calligraphy was like a god. Some people wondered why the wooden door was self-opened. After a long time, they realized that Mr. Mei had a daughter who was beautiful and intelligent, skilled in poetry and calligraphy. Whenever she heard the sound of pecking, she would get up and open the door, and then hide behind the door to let the guests in.

Mr. Mei was energetic, clear and elegant, and easy-going. He liked to play with children. When I was six or seven years old, Mr. Mei had a very close relationship with my uncle and grandfather. When he came to my house, he would always hold me and ask me to write. Later, I remembered my late grandmother saying: Whenever Mr. Mei wrote screen couplets, he would always ask my aunt to hold the paper, because my aunt also knew how to write. Mr. Mei liked to eat tea eggs, and he would not be full without eating more than a dozen of them. He also liked to eat glutinous rice. After eating, he would say and walk, "I can fly! I can fly!" And his calligraphy was even better at this time.

Mr. Mei was poor. Every year when the end of the year came, he would come to Shanghai. Wealthy merchants and officials, those who heard of his name, would ask him to write. Mr. Mei sometimes agreed and sometimes did not. Someone gave him a fur coat, and he pretended to ask Mr. Mei to try it on, and laughed and said: This coat fits Mr. Mei's figure very well. Mr. Mei does not need to buy another one, so as to avoid the incompatibility of the axe handle. Mr. Mei smiled and accepted it. After Mr. Mei returned, the money from selling his calligraphy came in steadily, and Mr. Mei passed the end of the year safely.

One day, Mr. Mei passed by the Fourth Horse Road and saw women in white powder and black eyebrows coming and going on the road. Mr. Mei shouted loudly in the crowd of women: "Niang Niang! Niang Niang!" (Ningbo dialect: Let me pass!) Those who heard it laughed.

Mr. Mei's calligraphy is rarely passed down to this day. Those who get a small piece of silk or paper treasure it like a treasure. In the recent hundred years, there is no calligrapher in the country who can surpass him.

Wooden Fish 157

— Zhang Yide

In today's society, the most beloved literature of old-fashioned women remains "Drum Lyrics" and "Stringed Ballads," because refined and beautiful literature fails to interest them. Only "Drum Lyrics" and "Stringed Ballads" can move their heartstrings, causing these women to unconsciously shed countless tears.

However, the "Stringed Ballads" favored by Guangdong women are not quite the same as the common ones. They have created a separate term for them called "Wooden Fish." The difference with "Wooden Fish" is that they are not as long as Stringed Ballads, nor do they have as many elaborate, conversational asides. To give a precise analogy, Stringed Ballads are like long, episodic novels, while Wooden Fish are like short literary essays. Although Wooden Fish also contain purely rational or lyrical passages, this is only a small part. The majority still resembles a story poem in form.

Wherever you go, as long as you are within the boundaries of Guangzhou, you can hear old-fashioned women singing these tunes while working or chatting. If you meet an acquaintance who is an old-fashioned woman, and you ask her, "Can you sing Wooden Fish?" then she will likely answer you, "I can, but I don't sing very well." As a result, she will sing you the popular Wooden Fish about Xue Mei sacrificing at the grave: "My husband has died, and my tears have not yet dried; the Qingming Festival is near, adding more sorrow; I prepare paper money to burn at the graveside, lest this mountain valley be neglected..."

The Wooden Fish they sing does not have a fixed rhythm or pitch. It goes up and down along with the tones of the words. Sometimes when they sing with great emotion, in the sad and melancholic places, they release the emotions that have accumulated deep in their hearts, along with the melody, sobbing and weeping.

The lyrics in Wooden Fish are mostly composed in the Guangdong dialect and are spoken from a woman's perspective. The content of the lyrics also tends to lean toward the mournful and tragic. The lyrics are so sad and unbearable to hear that when you listen to them sing Wooden Fish, the sorrow in your heart is already evident in your expression.

Night Notes from Volcano 158

— Mu Liang

The city's night is not as silent and simple as the countryside. Splendid and colorful neon lights, stained with what seems like blood, hide on shop signs or corners, blinking their eyes. Dashing through the shadows are the insane machines of the new century: such as the 1934 model "Studebaker," "Black Puma Skin," the 1935 models "Chrysler," "Plymouth," and so on... meandering long queues like a formation driving smoothly on the smooth, flat asphalt toward the magnificent Volcano, again and again… interlacing.

The Western-style uniformed "small attendants" open the glass doors of "Chrome" and let the enchanting Lucia girls, holding the hands of gentlemen, walk in. They step on the marble granite floor, their footsteps light, one group, another group, packing the place to the brim.

The bandstand begins to unleash the melody of music, and these couples from beyond the century slowly glide along the smooth floor, following the music. Dancing, kissing, embracing tightly, the intoxicating, moving beauty, is enjoyed and admired by the gentlemen.

During the break, bangs sound from the east, bangs sound from the west, the air of Volcano is filled with tense emotion—the caps of beer and champagne flying wildly.

The Lucia girls and the gentlemen raise their champagne glasses together, the grape wine inside, intoxicated by laughter and lascivious poses!

The bandstand unleashes the melody of music twenty-some times, and everyone's feet slowly glide along the smooth floor.

As soon as closing time arrives, the new-century machines become lively again on the asphalt. Some Lucia girls, however, follow the gentlemen to make pink dreams.

Therefore, the bustling and noisy Volcano finally becomes silent!

The Vague Records of Imperial Incense 159

— Originally by Princess Deling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Chapter 29: Imperial Physician

We stayed on the lake, and no one felt bored, almost until five or six o'clock in the afternoon, when it was getting dark before we stopped. Therefore, I seized the opportunity to ask the Empress Dowager what she meant by the "mischievous imp of fate" that she mentioned earlier. She already knew that I was someone who loved to ask questions, and she herself was someone who loved to explain everything to people. So, her reply came out with a smile without any hesitation.

"Strictly speaking, this is just a very peculiar belief! This belief is that people must not be too happy. If you are too happy, there will be a figure similar to a deity in the dark, who will suddenly descend upon you when you are least prepared, and cause you all kinds of unhappiness. It can also be said that an event that makes people feel unhappy is a kind of duty that this deity must fulfill. Because if it were not manipulating things, people would wantonly enjoy themselves, and would not know what pain and suffering are like. So, it is working all year round. If you already feel very comfortable and at ease, the mischievous imp of fate will come and make you feel uneasy and uncomfortable right away; or, if you are strutting and full of high spirits, it will come and make your happiness disappear into thin air. Its stomach is simply full of materials for playing pranks on people. No matter what the matter, while it is proceeding smoothly and steadily, it cannot avoid being disrupted by it a few times. Therefore, there is no truly smooth and steady thing in the world." (346)

Little Western Paradise 160

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 15: Sincere Words and Earnest Advice, Pounding the Table Out of Injustice; the Allure of Money and Lights, Pitifully Selling a Person

The last sentence, his voice was very loud, you could tell that he had made a great determination. When Bei Hai heard this, he clenched his teeth tightly. The newspaper held in both hands tore apart with a "嗤" sound. This was a newspaper provided by the hotel, so he had to put it down and find a waiter to say that he was willing to pay for the loss. Since he said so, the waiter naturally found it inconvenient to ask him for compensation, saying that it was worthless, and that was the end of it. But in the time it took to say these few words, when Bei Hai looked back, both women had left. He guessed that Mrs. Hu must have gone home to discuss Yue Ying's price. Although he and Yue Ying didn't have any friendship, in terms of human feelings, he felt that such a good girl was ultimately selling herself, which was really unbearable. As for the illusion that had formed in his mind these past few days, it had finally quickly become an illusion, which goes without saying. He couldn't bear this matter in his heart, so without thinking, he rushed straight to Cheng Zhiqian's room. Zhiqian was also reading a book. Seeing him rushing in angrily, he looked at him with the book in his hand, somewhat stunned. Bei Hai stopped at the door, his face red, and said: Mr. Cheng, I think this matter is too outrageous! Zhiqian's face also turned red, and he stood up and said: Why are you yelling at me, saying it's outrageous? I asked you to come for tutoring, I had no ill intentions. Moreover, whether you come or not is up to you, how can you say such a thing to me. As he said that, he slammed the book in his hand on the table. Bei Hai paused for a moment, then laughed: Ah! Mr. Cheng, you misunderstood. It's that in front of me, I saw something that I thought was too outrageous, so I came to report it to you. How could I not know what is good for me, how dare I offend Mr. Cheng. (246)

Social Sketches

A Murdered Woman (Part 2) 161

— You Aimei

In the distant aftermath of the [marriage] disturbance, how did she fare? Alas! She was a weakling who had been shaped through much suffering, with no awareness or ability to resist! She could only weep in secret!

She married in the autumn of that year. I remember when my father returned from her home on the day she returned to her parents' home, he sighed to my mother, "Alas! That child Qingzhang, she is so honest and pitiful!" I interjected and asked my father, "What does this mean?" Only then did I learn that on the second night after her marriage, her husband flattered her by taking out the photo that his former lover had given him and tearing it up in front of her. Moreover, he repented to her and said, "If our marriage had been a little earlier, I would not have had that previous misstep." When she returned to her parents' home, she secretly told her mother all these things, seeming very satisfied in her heart. Alas! How could she know that this is called forgetting the old when you get the new, and that this kind of person is the most unreliable? My father had deep experience, so he sighed like that!

Over the next two or three years, my family situation deteriorated. The winter before last, my father also passed away. The burden of life weighed on my shoulders, and I spent the whole year running around outside, trying to make a living. Therefore, I wasn't very clear about her situation. Last year, worried about the weather, I lost my job and went home. Coincidentally, she was also in the city, staying at her parents' home. At this time, she was already pregnant. Once, when I saw her, she suddenly said to me: she wanted to send something to my house, to see my mother. I went back and told my mother, and my mother also planned to ask her to come over for a chat. However, after she got married, she had never been to my house before. According to custom, we had to prepare a full banquet to treat her, and we couldn't just let her eat a regular meal. But my finances were in a panic. I had to tell her: "The weather is too hot, wait until it's cooler, and then I'll pick you up to play." But in just a few days, she had already returned to the countryside. Who knew that this parting would be our final farewell? In the autumn, I heard that she had given birth to a boy, but I also heard that her husband had changed his mind and often abused her. Although I couldn't help but feel sorry for her, I didn't expect that in this short half a year, her husband's attitude toward her would get worse and worse, and as a result, he would beat her until her body was covered in injuries! Logically, there are many concrete ways to deal with such a situation. However, how could someone with her personality and will, like her, think of or do those things? What's more, her parents' family was stubborn, and the realistic society was feudal. Their position was also under the leadership of old ethical teachings. How could they allow her to? If not, why wait until today? When the disturbance started before her marriage, they wouldn't have blindly pushed her into the pit of fire! So, she could only grieve for her short life, and lightly end her youth of only twenty-three years with a three-foot white silk.

Alas! The dead are gone! What else can be said! What is especially painful is that I look out at my hometown, where there are still many pitiful women, who are weaklings with the same illness as her, who are also succumbing to the control of old ethical teachings, enduring the sanctions of feudal society, and grieving in the shadows, waiting for them to be murdered!

Appendix: After I finished writing this article, I still have lingering sorrow, and my feelings are still uncontrollable. I cry for her with a couplet, which is also attached below.

The old events are too painful to mention again. We used to play together as children. When she came of age, I taught her how to write. My feelings for her were like that of a sibling. How could I bear the bad news from afar?

Meeting a person who was not good for her was tragic. Three feet of white silk. A mound of yellow earth. I pity my sister who died with her eyes closed. Who will complain of her grievances in the underworld?

Organizational Regulations

Organizational Regulations of the Shanghai Municipal Children's Year Implementation Committee, Article 1 This committee shall preside over all matters related to the Shanghai Municipal Children's Year in accordance with the provisions of Article 3 of the National Children's Year Implementation Measures Outline. Article 2 This committee shall be organized by representatives of the following agencies and groups: (1) One representative from the Secretariat of the Municipal Government; (2) Five representatives from the Social Affairs Bureau; (3) Five representatives from the Education Bureau; (4) Two representatives from the Public Security Bureau; (5) Two representatives from the Health Bureau; (6) Two representatives from the Charity Federation; (7) Two representatives from the Children's Happiness Committee; (8) Two representatives from the Chinese Children's Welfare Association. Article 3 This committee shall publicly elect three members as standing committee members to handle all affairs of this committee. Article 4 This committee shall hold a full meeting once a month and a standing committee meeting once every half month, and may convene temporary meetings when necessary. Article 5 The task of this committee is to comply with the National Children's Year Implementation Measures Outline and handle matters with reference to the situation in this city. Article 6 This committee may establish several staff members depending on the complexity of the affairs, and the relevant agencies and groups shall send personnel to serve. Article 7 This committee shall handle matters in groups, and the groups and their responsibilities shall be determined separately. Article 8 The members of this committee are all unpaid, but travel expenses may be paid at discretion for official travel, and staff may be given subsidies as necessary. Article 9 The office of this committee shall be located in the Social Affairs Bureau. Article 10 This committee shall begin its work in June 1935 and end in October 1936. Article 11 These regulations shall be implemented from the date they are submitted to the municipal government for approval and promulgation.

Introduction to the New Metal Vacuum Tube 209

— Meng Pin

Vacuum tubes are climbing the ladder of evolution, improving layer by layer, and now their shape is completely different from that of their ancestors. Recently, General Electric Company of the United States has manufactured a metal vacuum tube that is smaller than the usual glass tube. It has a metal shell on the outside, which not only serves as a shielding cover, but also has several advantages, including strong structure, fast heat dissipation, reduced internal capacity, and economic cost.

It is said that ten different types of these vacuum tubes have now been created, including powerful rectifier tubes, triode output tubes, variable mu pentodes, pentagrid converters, and hexodes. The last one is composed of a small triode and a twin diode, with two cathodes and duo-plates, but its height (the height above the lamp waist) is only 1 1/2 inches.

The socket of this new vacuum tube is also more advanced than the previous socket. Regardless of the number of pins on the vacuum tube, it can be inserted into the same eight-pin socket, because the pin spacing is exactly the same and at a certain interval. In the center of the vacuum tube, there is a large pin with a key installed on it. If we want to insert the tube into the socket, we only need to insert the large pin into the large hole in the middle of the socket first, and then slowly rotate the vacuum tube until the key on the large pin falls into the corresponding slot, and then insert the vacuum tube. In this way, there is no need to recognize the thickness of the pins like ordinary vacuum tubes, so even in dark places, the vacuum tube can be inserted into the socket without making mistakes. In addition to the pins that should be present, there is one more pin, which is connected to the external shield, so the spring in the corresponding hole on the socket should be grounded.

Because these vacuum tubes do not have glass pillars inside, the structure is much simpler. Also, because the terminals of each electrode are led out from the bottom plate, the lead wires are short and strong, and the internal capacity is greatly reduced. As for its manufacturing method, it is different from the usual one. Here, we start from the bottom plate, and after each electrode is installed, the lead wires are led out from the bottom plate. Before the lead wires are led out, a small circle made of alloy is soldered into the holes in the bottom plate. This alloy is specially made to suit the needs here. Its name is Fernicc, made of iron, nickel, and cobalt. The expansion coefficient is the same as glass. The lead-out wire passes through a small glass bead, and then the glass bead is melted into the alloy ring.

The outer shell of the vacuum tube is made of 1/58 inch thick iron sheet and is used for shielding. Inside the outer shell, there is also a cylinder, which is equivalent to the glass cover of an ordinary vacuum tube. The joint between this cylinder and the bottom plate uses the principle of electric welding. A strong current of 20,000 amperes is passed through it for 1/4 second, and the cylinder around and the bottom plate are welded tightly. After welding, after the air exclusion procedure, the structure of the vacuum tube is almost complete. As for the air that is not completely removed from the tube, it cannot be treated according to the usual method using the high-frequency induction coil method. A strong gas flame should be used to burn it until it turns red.

The metal vacuum tubes mentioned above are not yet sold on the market, but it is said that these new products will be used in various full-wave radios operated by General Electric Company in the United States.

Twelve-Pin Vacuum Tube 210

— Pao

A German magazine, Funk-Technische Monatsliefte Magazine, talks about an exciting new product, which is a set of complex vacuum tubes with twelve pins manufactured by D.S. Loewe Co., Germany.

Such a vacuum tube has two characteristics: first, in addition to the original screen grid and filament in the vacuum tube, sometimes there are also resistors and other components connected inside. For example, in a grid-leak detection vacuum tube, the grid leak and grid fixed capacitor are already connected in the vacuum tube during manufacturing, making it particularly simple to be used in radios. Second, all vacuum tubes, regardless of their number, have twelve pins. For example, if a certain vacuum tube only needs nine pins, the remaining three pins are left unused. Therefore, any vacuum tube can be equipped with the same tube socket. (This point can be imitated when China manufactures its own vacuum tubes.) Also, there are three protrusions on the base of the vacuum tube to prevent it from being inserted incorrectly into the tube socket.

In addition to the filament being shared, each electrode of this type of complex vacuum tube is completely independent. When used, it is no different from two or three separate vacuum tubes. There are now four types that have been produced: A, radio frequency pentode and grid-leak detection tube (leakage and capacitor have been connected in the tube). B, radio frequency pentode and diode detection tube and screen grid tetrode. C, pentode mixer tube and triode oscillator tube and pentode intermediate frequency amplifier tube. D, radio frequency pentode and screen grid detection tube and pentode power amplifier tube. Among the above types, type C is specially for superheterodyne use, and type D can be widely used in radios with one vacuum tube and a loudspeaker.

Single-Tube AC/DC "Radio Phonograph Adapter" 211

— Liu Tongkang

— New Application of 12A7 Compound Vacuum Tube —

In the 71st issue of this journal, there was an article by Mr. Ming Xiang, "Radio Phonograph Adapter". The function of this machine is actually a small-power transmitter. The author was also interested and imitated it. Due to parts, the oscillation tube used a DC 33, which had a good effect, but the power consumption was very large—

The one introduced here is made using only one new compound vacuum tube 127, which functions as both oscillation and rectification. According to the test, the results are similar to the previous two, but there are very few auxiliary equipment, and the power is taken from AC/DC, so it is convenient to use and easy to manage, which is most suitable for comrades who love economy.

The attached diagram is the circuit of this adapter. The entire machine is placed in a metal box and grounded to prevent the transmitted radio waves from interfering with nearby radios. The C voltage is obtained by dropping the voltage of the screen grid current and screen grid current through R. R uses a variable resistor, which is better as a regulator than a fixed one.

When using, connect the A and G terminals of this device to the antenna and ground terminals of the radio, respectively. Then connect the control grid and cathode of this device (as shown by the dotted line X in the figure), and adjust the radio to a silent place (a place without a radio station). Then adjust the variable capacitor C in this device. As soon as the X dotted line is removed and the pickup is connected, it is ok! (However, it should be noted that the pickup should use a high-impedance type, otherwise a transformer must be connected.) Applied parts.

C 0005MFD Variable capacitor

C1C2C3 8MFD Electrolytic capacitor

R 5000Ω Variable resistor

R1 330Ω50w Fixed resistor

V 12A7 Compound vacuum tube

AFC 30H25MA Low frequency choke coil

L 30

L1 54T

(The above two coils, H, are wound with No. 28 enameled wire on a one-and-a-half inch diameter plastic tube. L1 is wound with force wire on a two-inch diameter. A head is drawn at 27 turns. H is placed inside L1.)

Current Status of Soviet Amateur Radio (Continued) 212

— Yan Qingzhi

The Radio Friends Association meets once every winter to discuss technical issues and provide sufficient courses to professor demands. Most of the "Shortwave Department" report the results of their experiments and the achievements of their activities, and they publish "Amateur Short Notes" (Ham Sheet). This magazine is valued by amateurs. Q symbols and general amateur abbreviations are also written in Russian on it.

The most popular radio magazine with the largest number of readers is "Radio Front". This magazine is published twice a month and contains a shortwave column, which records words and letters of particular interest to amateurs. There are technical columns, as well as records of radio news and amateur radio stations, etc.

It is very common to install the equipment of members in clubs or organizations, because there is no cost for installing the equipment, so ordinary people who can live a normal life can set it up themselves. The money paid is government-circulated banknotes that have no exchange value externally, and domestic workers call it, "Haipa, Ruble". Therefore, important machines must use domestic products, and parts such as electric meters can also be manufactured by themselves. Amateurs use the things they make themselves.

There are many radio shops on the street that sell parts and various accessories. Many things are new, and many are very old.

Radios usually use regenerative detection. It is also common to see loudspeakers installed at the entrance of stores. Few people listen to the broadcast. Most of them are used for publicity, especially at large train stations. Radios are usually simple designs with two or three tubes. Regenerative detection and a one-stage low-frequency amplification two-tube machine is very common, and the three-tube machine usually adds a stage of tunable high-frequency amplification.

Transmitters also use very simple styles. There are also many amateurs who use crystal control. Most of the styles are grid-shelf or panel style. Transmitting vacuum tubes generally use 20 watts to 150 watts. Antennas generally use American-style single-wire feed.

Since June last year, all Soviet amateurs have revised the regions, and their call signs have also been changed.

Amateur radio stations are listened to with very little tax, which includes some special donations. In addition, the sending and receiving of telegrams must be transferred through the "Central Bureau of Shortwave Department" and the local shortwave department. Communication with other countries uses the language of the "International Amateur League". That is, domestic amateurs also use the language for mutual communication. For example, "TCF" means ordinary telegram, and in the Soviet Union, it is used to mean QSO (communication).

Finally, let me briefly talk about the situation of broadcasting stations. There is a Moscow Broadcasting Station 35 kilometers north of Moscow, using 16 50,000-watt water-cooled vacuum tubes. The antenna power is about 100,000 watts, and the last stage uses Class B amplification.

In the same room, there is also a 20,000-watt transmitter. (End)

Introduction to Volume 1, Issue 11 of the Philips Wireless Magazine 213

I recently received a gift of Volume 1, Issue 11 of the Philips Wireless Magazine published by Philips Foreign Company at 133 Sichuan Road, Shanghai on the 15th of this month. It contains a detailed manufacturing method of the latest energy-saving battery radio, starting from the method of winding coils, parts layout, and straight to how to start the whole machine after assembly. Each section is explained with detailed diagrams, and the text is simple and detailed. Even those who have no experience in wireless can read this article and make a radio with excellent results. It has the same wonderful effect as the industrial lamp machine manufacturing method published in the ninth issue of the magazine, and the attached ring history is more detailed. In addition, there are wireless elementary discussion and wireless terminology review, etc., all written by Mr. Cheng Yikun, the editor-in-chief of the magazine (note: Mr. is a member of the World Wireless Engineer Society). Finally, there is also a "Wireless Little Brain" that specializes in the simple manufacturing and design methods of various parts used in various wireless radios. Readers can make various sophisticated parts with very ordinary materials. It is a must-have reference book for amateur wireless researchers. Moreover, the magazine is promoting wireless, so the price is extremely low (the annual subscription of 12 issues is only one yuan and five cents in silver dollars. Postage stamps are calculated at 90% of the silver dollar value, and an additional 10 cents for postage outside the local area). The printing is excellent and the decoration is beautiful. All readers of this newspaper who state that they are introduced by Mr. Xiao Xiuqing or Mr. Qin Ximin of this newspaper can not only avoid postage outside the local area, but also use postage stamps at full value, so I am happy to introduce it.
