Complete Westernization? Colonialization? 215

— Ye Qing

The fact that China is under imperialist aggression is now recognized by everyone, although Dr. Hu Shi once regarded it as an incredible tale. Regarding the method of aggression, the European and American factions covet money and advocate turning China into an economic colony; the Eastern faction covets land even more, so they advocate turning China into a political colony. As for the faction that promotes imperialist culture (that is, Western culture) within China, they go a step further than the previous two factions and advocate turning China into a cultural colony. Their slogan is complete Westernization.

The former faction seizes our markets, the middle faction seizes our land, and the latter faction seizes our spirit. The so-called seizing our spirit, in old words, is seizing our hearts. Comparing the gains and losses of these three factions, the latter faction is the fiercest. Because after imperialist culture dominates our consciousness, we will reach a state of dead hearts and will never be able to turn over. Hu Shi does not understand abstract nouns such as imperialism, and both subjectively and objectively defends it, which is because his consciousness has been imperialized.

Therefore, the theory of complete Westernization is a theory of surrender to imperialism in the ideological world and a theory of cultural colonization.

The initiator of this theory is Hu Shi, an international scholar created by the material and spiritual pillars of European and American international imperialism. This can be understood by simply reading his article "Our Attitude Towards Modern Western Civilization". Today, Chen Xujing and Liang Shiqiu, etc., have succeeded him. They go a step further and advocate obliterating China itself, saying that it can only imitate imperialist culture. Liang Shiqiu even made it clear that we cannot create, and advocating creation is megalomania (Dagong Daily, June 9 this year). This is tantamount to saying that the Chinese are only worthy of being coolies and compradors for imperialist culture.

In this case, are our introduction work wrong? It was progressive in the past and had the value of literary revival; now, after "1927", it is a conservative thing. In the fundamental sense, it had creative value in the past (relatively), and it was regarded as a means (for the sake of absolute creation); now, it is willing to introduce and opposes creation.

Such an introduction does not have the meaning of a cultural enlightenment movement, but the meaning of a cultural colonization. The Chinese consciousness should not be independent and free to create, but can only be subordinate to the West.

But, according to you, can China create culture? Yes. France in the 18th century was more backward than England at that time. They introduced Locke, but created a more thorough epistemology than Locke; introduced Newton, but created a more perfect worldview than Newton. Germany in the 18th and 19th centuries was more backward than England and France at that time, but Kant, Fichte, Schelling, Hegel and other great philosophers and Marx, Engels and other great thinkers appeared. Russia in the 20th century was more backward than England, France and Germany. However, today, since 1917, it has become the pioneer of the world's new culture—socialist culture. It is simply a law that backward countries have contributions in culture.

Why? There is only one reason, that is, starting from the cutting edge of historical development. To put it plainly, it starts from the direction of development implied by advanced countries. To put it in words that everyone knows, it is "catching up from the front." For example, if the power engine of industry has gone from water to steam to electricity in advanced countries, then you should go straight ahead from electricity. This can leave room for creativity. Starting from water is called following along, and you can only imitate and cannot create forever.

In this way, in order to have a creative effect in culture, one must start from socialism. Because it is something that is just emerging in the West and urgently needs people to exert their creativity. This is why Russia has moved to the forefront of world cultural history. If our introduction starts from capitalism and is only satisfied with capitalism, then there is absolutely no creativity. Because capitalism has gone through 300 years in the West. Now, it has gone from germination to development to aging, and there is no room for creation. Introducing this kind of culture is obviously taking a downward path.

What Hu Shi, Chen Xujing, Liang Shiqiu, etc. introduced is superficially Western culture, but in fact it is capitalist culture—imperialist culture. They follow along, and they will only follow in other people's footsteps for the rest of their lives, so they certainly don't feel creativity. Therefore, Hu Shi openly advocated imitation and said that imitation is creation ("Independent Review" No. 13). Chen Xujing's complete Westernization is complete imitation. Liang Shiqiu then vilified creation as megalomania.

Such imitation is a cultural surrender. Chinese nation, fall into the arms of imperialism. If it wants to turn you into an economic colony and a political colony, then you should go one step further and become a cultural colony!

We who oppose imperialism do not agree. We demand economic independence and freedom, political independence and freedom, and even more cultural independence and freedom. If the first two demands are a kind of practical behavior, and the latter is a kind of conscious activity, and human behavior must pass through consciousness, then the demand for cultural independence and freedom is the beginning of relieving economic oppression and political oppression, that is, the entire oppression. It represents the awakening of the Chinese nation.

After eighty or ninety years of oppression, especially after the "September 18th Incident", the "January 28th Incident", and the "Hebei Issue", advocating cultural independence and freedom is a spiritual protest of intellectuals. No, it is still the new beginning of the Chinese nation's unwillingness to succumb after the new oppression and demand for the independence and freedom of the entire organization.

Down with the foreign compradors in the cultural circle!

Create a new culture from the cutting edge of historical development!

"Germany in 1848" 216

— Li Jianfang

New Life Publishing Company Price 6 Jiao

—One of the History Reading Notes—

"Germany in 1848," also known as "Revolution and Counter-Revolution." In the past, this book was generally thought to be written by Marx, but since the publication of the Marx-Engels correspondence, people have learned that the book was actually written by Engels. This is a famous work on the study of the German Revolution of 1848. The editor of this book, Eleanor Marx (Marx's daughter), said that this book and Marx's "The Eighteenth Brumaire of Louis Bonaparte" are unparalleled, and she is absolutely right.

I read this book a long time ago. This time, because I wanted to make a comparative study of German history from the 17th and 18th centuries and the early 19th century with the history of China in the last hundred years, I read the book again in detail. After reading this book this time, I not only felt that the modern history of China and the history of Germany from 1523 to 1848 have many similarities, but also discovered that the German Revolution of 1848 and the Chinese Revolution of 1911 also have many similarities.

Before 1848, Germany was a country with many small feudal states. Before 1911, China was also like that. Before 1848, Germany was a country dominated by France and Russia. Before 1911, China was also like that. In 1848, the power of the feudal princes in Germany was higher than that of the German middle class at that time. In 1911, China was also like that.

The Revolution of 1848 failed. The reason for the failure was naturally due to the feudal lords' opposition to nationalism and the weakness and incompetence of the German middle class. Therefore, the Revolution of 1848 not only failed to unify Germany, but led to great division. The most obvious manifestation of this division was that Austria, which shared the same race and culture, completely separated from Germany and became independent. This was the result of 1848, and this result is very similar to our Revolution of 1911. However, Germany was better than China at that time. On the one hand, the development of capitalism in Germany in 1848 seemed to be higher than that in China. On the other hand, Germany in 1848 did not have as much surplus population as China in 1911. Therefore, the Revolution of 1848 only led to the independence of Austria, and did not lead to a Chinese-style warlord civil war. However, according to Engels, this possibility was fully present at that time.

As for China, because of its vast land area, weak capitalist development, the existence of a large surplus population, and the formation of centrifugal forces in local military groups against the central government, the Revolution of 1911 directly became a signal for warlord wars. Naturally, many of the civil wars after the Revolution of 1911 were caused by imperialist powers wanting to compete for spheres of influence in China, but if China did not have a foundation for imperialism to exploit, even imperialism could not cause civil wars.

China's internal wars in the past decades were based on the struggle between the Manchu Qing Empire and the Hong Yang uprising. In order to fight against the Hong Yang uprising, the Manchu Qing Empire had to allow local landlords to freely train troops, and in order to save the central government's financial shortages, it had to allow local landlords to freely set up Likin checkpoints. This situation is exactly the same as the situation after the German Peasants' Revolt in 1523. The German Peasants' War was the beginning of the ebb of German history, and the Chinese Hong Yang Uprising was also the beginning of the ebb of Chinese history. The German Peasants' Revolt directly led to the German local princes' struggle against central centralization, leading to the Thirty Years' War from 1618 to 1648. The result of the Chinese Hong Yang Uprising led to the warlord civil wars of the past ten years. According to Engels, the result of the German Thirty Years' War was that Germany completely withdrew from the historical stage of European national political activities for two hundred years. The social consequences of the Chinese Peasants' War also made it impossible for China to rise up in the past sixty or seventy years.

When in 1848, according to Engels, there were three paths to German unification:

The first was to overthrow all the numerous states and achieve true unification, that is, the path of open revolution.

The second was unification under the leadership of Austria.

The third was unification under the leadership of Prussia.

As we know, the first and second paths both failed, and later Germany realized the third path.

How was this third path realized? As everyone knows, this was the result of Bismarck's iron-blood policy. Although the Revolution of 1848 failed, German capitalism did not stop as a result. On the contrary, from 1848 to 1863, German capitalism developed faster than Chinese capitalism after 1911. Because of this development, Bismarck was able to obtain the support of the middle class to unify Germany. The two wars that Bismarck waged in 1864 and 1866 for unification were of revolutionary significance. These wars were not fundamentally different from the Northern Expedition in China from 1925 to 1927. On the contrary, their historical significance was very similar.

Bismarck's victory symbolized the regaining of national unity by Germany. Although this unification was completed by the upper class, it had a very important significance for the development of the German nation. In 1866, when Bismarck had indeed achieved victory over Austria, Germany's greatest enemy at that time was France. At this time, France's obstruction of German unification was just like Japan's obstruction of Chinese unification now.

At that time, France was ruled by Napoleon III, whose policy was to try to keep Germany divided. He wanted Germany to retain the situation of being ruled by many small states so that he could manipulate it from the middle. Therefore, German unification would inevitably force Germany to go to war with France. The Franco-Prussian War broke out in 1870. As a result, Prussia defeated France, and the unified German Empire was completely established.

From the study of German history, can we make some kind of diagnosis of the current situation in China? This is what I think is most worthy of our attention.

Impressions of Various Bookstores (Continued) 217

— Li Hengzhi

Sixteen, Yadong Bookstore

Yadong Bookstore, which started with textual research, punctuation of old novels, really made a little fortune in the past few years. Yadong's success (naturally only refers to making money) was really a fluke. Because, after the New Youth era, Hu Shi was "very popular", and several collections of Hu Shi's essays were published by Yadong. At the same time, old vernacular novels were more valued by the general public because of the vernacular movement. Moreover, with the addition of the textual research and punctuation of Dr. Hu, the "initiator" (?) of the vernacular movement, it would inevitably be even more valuable than Luoyang paper (at that time, there were many such old novels, and students in the more stubborn middle and primary schools could only secretly read them. Since Dr. Hu advocated them, many were adopted as extracurricular reading materials or supplementary readers). And these books were all published by Yadong Bookstore. With the success of Lu Xun alone, the current "Beixin" was produced. How could Yadong not make a fortune at that time?

Each bookstore with a smaller scope, due to the subjective decisions of the host or the person in charge of the editorial department, will often form a system or characteristic in publishing. However, Yadong, except for punctuating old novels, does not have such a system or characteristic. Yadong's new books are not few, there are dozens of them. Among them, some are monographs on social sciences such as dialectics, and some are inexplicably "Week X" school of literature. You only need to look through Yadong's circular book catalog to know the incompetence of the editorial department of the bookstore, or that the host is simply a bookseller who does not understand publishing.

Soon, crudely made new culture publishing houses and other punctuated books competed for sales, and a tide of punctuated books with discounts of 20%, 30% and even 40% surged behind. A bookstore without a publishing strategy would inevitably be at a loss.

Seventeen Women's Bookstore

Shanghai's bookstores are usually gathered in the Qipan Street area of Fuzhou Road, but there are also exceptions. The Women's Bookstore is located in the middle of many massage parlors in Xiahui Road. This is the deepest impression that the Women's Bookstore gives our readers. Secondly, it is the name "Women's Bookstore", but it is only this name. The "Women's Library" and "Women's Monthly" published by it seem to be far from the former Commercial Press's "Women's Magazine" and the enlightened "New Woman". However, publications such as "Women's Magazine" and "New Woman" are not only mostly edited and written by men, but also mostly read by men. Therefore, given the backwardness of women's knowledge level, "Women's Monthly" is enough to show that it is a reading material for women. And "Women's Voice", which often shows its neck and shoulders in newspaper advertisements now, is just like this, and can be called a pair of sister flowers with "Women's Monthly". However, recently, Ms. Huang Xinmian, the editor of "Women's Monthly" and "Women's Library", passed away due to illness. The host of the Women's Bookstore is no longer a woman, but Mr. Yao Mingda, a man. Perhaps the Women's Bookstore and the books it publishes will have considerable reforms in the future.

Eighteen New China Bookstore

"The New China" has a short history and is now in silence. The New China did not give us much to pay attention to in the past, but when Kaiming moved to a new location and the New China moved into the old site of Kaiming, it did attract everyone's attention a little. However, since the establishment of the retail department, the New China has become increasingly silent.

The first book published by the New China is the Literary Series, followed by children's books. In addition, few new books are published. These two types of books are very "adapted to the trend" because other bookstores are publishing this type of book at this time. Because of this, the New China had to remain silent because the Literary Series and children's books of the New China lagged behind others, and it itself had few characteristics that could be rushed forward. It is very regrettable for such a bookstore because it gains nothing in terms of "profit" and "promoting culture".

Shenbao Local Supplement

Talks

Relief and Prevention of Drought 218

— Meng Ruo

The unfortunate Chinese peasants have had to live under the scourge of natural and man-made disasters every year in recent years. Since the beginning of summer this year, drought conditions have formed in various places, either due to lack of rain or drying up of rivers and canals. Recently, reports of disaster conditions from various provinces have been flooding in. It is reported that the rivers in Henan Province are dry and the sand is blowing, the wind and hail in Jiangsu Province are causing disasters, black frost has fallen repeatedly in Shaanxi Province, floods and hailstorms have occurred in Anhui Province, floods have occurred in Fujian Province, and strong winds and rain have caused disasters in Chahar Province. From this, it can be seen that the drought and disaster conditions in various places have not only not been alleviated, but also tend to be more dangerous. The general peasants are once again trapped in deep water and scorching heat. If relief and prevention are not planned early, the rural areas will inevitably go from decline to collapse in the future. The future of the national economy is really unimaginable.

The relief measures naturally only hope that the government authorities and various charitable organizations will work together to carry out. Provide disaster-stricken areas in various provinces with relief grain so that countless victims will not have to eat bark and grass roots or wait to die of starvation. May patriotic compatriots across the country take compassion as their guide, do their best, and donate generously to save a generation of innocent victims. As the saying goes, be prepared for danger in times of peace. Once the rural areas go bankrupt, the collapse of the cities will inevitably follow. Everyone must not regard the cries of the victims in various places as irrelevant and fail to provide assistance.

As for prevention, this work is also very urgent. Although drought is a natural disaster, it can be prevented. But as the Westerners say, human power can overcome nature. If we can find ways to dredge rivers and canals in places where drought has already appeared, in order to prepare for a rainy day, we may be able to remedy the situation. Otherwise, if we allow the drought to strike, there will be no hope for the autumn harvest, and the lives of many poor peasants will be even more insecure.

In addition, once a drought occurs in the rural areas, unscrupulous grain merchants will take advantage of the fire to rob. Either hoarding goods for speculation or raising grain prices. Its impact on general public food is extremely harmful. Therefore, it is hoped that the authorities will also pay close attention to this situation and strictly prohibit unscrupulous merchants from manipulating grain to relieve the people's difficulties.

Lodging 219

— Mo Jia

Because of an unexpected event, I hastily left home and ran to this place in the countryside on the same afternoon to live.

Perhaps it is due to recalling the past and unconsciously increasing a lot of cordiality in the mood of parting. When I arrived on the first day, the host greeted me with extremely strong emotions and sincere attitude, which made me feel very comforted - I had a place to stay temporarily. As dusk approached, without me saying anything, the host seemed to understand and prepared a bed for me.

"Maybe I will stay for a few more days," I declared.

"It doesn't matter, stay as long as you want," the host replied sincerely.

In the evening, the lights were turned off and we slept in our quilts, still talking incessantly about the different encounters during the years of separation, and recalling the various interesting and nostalgic memories of middle school. When we felt that we had finished talking and were a little sleepy, we fell asleep in a daze.

So I settled down casually.

When I encountered an unfortunate situation in my own territory, and I was very poor, being able to obtain a place to eat and sleep was the first thing that I couldn't accept was having to get up very early every day and go to bed very early at night - the host still maintained the lifestyle habits of a student, and it would be very painful for me, who had been immersed in the metropolis for a long time and had all the characteristics of a city dweller, to change all of a sudden. Although I tried my best to do it, I couldn't change it after all, and I still got up late and went to bed late every day. At first, the host seemed to be because of my initial arrival and didn't make any indication. After a few days, he said to me with a very serious face:

"Isn't this kind of life too decadent? Why have you become like this?" At the same time, a nearly arrogant smile appeared on his face, thinking that he was not decadent.

"It's become a habit. For the past few years since I started writing articles, my life has been like this. I know it's decadent, but I can't help it."

I had to give in to cater to his tone, but I felt a little ridiculous in my heart for his such simple-minded views.

So the host, who was easily pleased, smiled triumphantly again.

Being easily pleased and easily angered is exactly the host's consistent temperament. I was clear about his impulsive nature since we were middle school classmates, and it hasn't changed at all. In his words and actions, he always likes to reveal a boast of being smart and knowing more things than others. Whenever he discusses a problem with his family, it is often just casual talk and laughter, but the result is often a bitter mutual slander and malicious quarrel, until they all leave with blue faces and resentment. Therefore, when we talk about China, no matter what, there will be no conflict or anger, because every time I let him occupy all the benefits of the argument.

I know that living in someone else's home, just eating and sleeping, needs to eliminate myself as much as possible in any way, belittle myself, and even bury all my personality and thoughts, in order to accommodate everything of the host and earn good feelings and intimacy. Because of this, my spirit has increased a burden of suffering forced by the environment.

Why do I have to be like this, just because I live in someone else's home.

A month passed quickly. Tomorrow I will leave here. Although I have to worry about work, the pain of wearing shackles of spiritual unfreedom is even greater than the pain of worrying about work. And in the end, I still have to bid farewell to the host with a mouthful of gratitude: "These days, I have been treated kindly, and I have bothered you enough. Thank you."

Fortunately, tomorrow the shackles on my spirit can be removed.

A Story of Country Living 220

— Ling Ying

Under the south window is the courtyard of the new residence. Two rows of low-lying winter green trees sandwich a flower path paved with herringbone bricks. Near the stone altar are four parasol trees, which were newly planted last spring. Because of the gardener's kind cultivation, the trunks have grown taller than the building windows. The large chestnuts, like umbrellas, sway lightly in front of the window. I think about the owner's deliberate embellishment, but now I am enjoying it at the lowest rental price.

Last year, when I came out of the hospital, the doctor advised me to live in the countryside, but because of my profession, I could never leave the city. However, the determination to live in the country was laid in my heart at that time. This time, I accidentally found this suburban residence and moved in very smoothly.

The owner of the house is an old woman in her fifties. When my wife first visited, she babbled for half a day in such a frank manner. She told my wife that her son had disappeared after a failure in the stock exchange. Her property was used to repay her son's debts, leaving only this suburban house and an eight-year-old grandson and an old servant living here. She said more shamefully that the countryside was too lonely, and at the same time, she wanted to increase a little income to help the household. At the suggestion of the old servant, she posted an advertisement to recruit a formal co-resident.

The next day we agreed with each other and moved in. The house is a row of three rooms, two entrances. We rented the front entrance. If we wanted to rent the same house in the city, I am afraid it would be more than three or four times the rent.

We kept the middle room as our own bedroom, the left side was for the child and the nanny, and the right side agreed with my wife's opinion to set up a guest room. She said that although it takes an hour by bus to reach Shanghai, it is inconvenient for friends and relatives to come and go after all. Living in the countryside without a place for guests to stay overnight seems to be against the rules.

The hall downstairs in the middle is for public use. I made the room on the right a study. I longed for a quiet study where I could lock myself in and read a little bit. This wish has now been realized. When we moved in, the owner was surprised that I had so much luggage. In fact, most of it was my books. The old family servant asked if I was "a teacher," perhaps for this reason too.

The room on the left is naturally a reception room. Fortunately, the owner lent us many pieces of furniture, otherwise, moving from a living room where we lived, ate, and dressed, and now we have to distribute it to five rooms, it would be an excellent joke.

That night, we finished arranging it a little bit. The owner came over with her grandson and said a few words in Mandarin. She repeated yesterday's story. Older people like to talk a lot. Now it seems that she has a counterpart. She almost exclusively talked about her family's history. In the end, she cried with sobs. This made me feel a little dissatisfied. If she recites the story of her son doing stock exchange whenever she has the opportunity, it is really too embarrassing. She has been greatly stimulated, and reciting it like that seems to relieve a little pain. However, this pain will be transferred to others. To put it jokingly, it is also not suitable for my purpose of recuperating.

My wife listened attentively and said many comforting words, just like a mother comforting a child who had been beaten and cried back home. Although I didn't insert a word of exclamation about this story from beginning to end, I leaned against the window, staring blankly at the bright moon moving from the clouds. The courtyard was like being covered with a piece of broken brocade, fantasizing that the owner's son was a great businessman who was good at management, with flexible wrists, a mind that was good at thinking, and a wide body with a fat face. Perhaps he had a small beard. That kind of person failed in the stock exchange and left behind his elderly mother, who was babbling about this indelible history. And the villa was being enjoyed by such an ordinary person. A tragic scene of suicide seemed to float before my eyes, but the old man still hoped that her son would return!

When she was leaving, she said to my wife, "My son graduated from university. If he comes back, he will definitely get along well with Mr. Ling."

I watched her back as she went downstairs, feeling dazed and not relieved. I poured out two sleeping pills from the medicine bottle. I was afraid that I would have insomnia tonight.

Page 19

I watched her back as she went downstairs, and my heart was blank and not relieved. I poured out two sleeping pills from the medicine bottle. I was afraid that I would have insomnia tonight.

The Lonely One 221

— Especially

It was night, and all around was silence.

This house must have been built five or six years ago, wouldn't you say? The walls were so black, the original whiteness long gone, and speckled with dots. From a distance, some might mistake them for patterns, but in fact, they were the remains of small creatures that appeared with the season.

The weather, in the season when the sun was nearly equatorial, made the ground oily during the day, and this cage-like house had the sweltering heat of a steamer. The people living inside felt suffocated.

But the stifling feeling was not very long-lasting. When the cool evening breeze gently blew, this square house did not lose its blessing due to its size. However, no matter how worthless the place was, life was still precious. Therefore, to preserve this precious life, the windows had to be closed before going to sleep.

Somehow, with a heart devoured by fatigue, it was almost impossible to fall asleep immediately upon lying in bed. Thinking about the things of the day, the arrogant faces, and how to work the next day, the heart became particularly uneasy.

Pushing open the only window, the high sky was a black expanse, without the seductive stars or the silvery moon. The fields below were dense, as if holding back rain.

In the light breeze, a burst of crying came, sharp and shrill!

—Spare me, ah, heavens… It was mournful, like a child being beaten.

Unable to resist, the weary mood was invigorated a bit. Leaning on the window, it was very quiet, without a single disturbing sound. The cold air blew, both here and there.

Perhaps it was the response to being beaten? Gradually, the sound grew louder, and the mournful element became particularly strong. It sounded familiar, and I realized it was the woman across the street punishing the servant she bought, Ah Rong.

It seemed as if some force was gripping me. Listening, a gust of cold wind hit me, and when I closed my eyes, countless sparks flashed and danced before my face.

Suddenly, the sparks parted to both sides, revealing an uneven face, a small body, tattered clothes, sallow and thin skin, throbbing and swollen eyes and nose, and a state of mingled fear and terror.

The beatings, of course, would not end there. On the contrary, from the crisp sounds, it was clear that they were even more severe. But somehow, the cries of sorrow could no longer be heard. All that could be heard was rapid scolding and rebuke.

The distant lights flickered on and off as the leaves swayed.

When the sunset once again streamed into my room, I dragged my heavy feet into the alley, but where was Ah Rong? She was nowhere to be seen. Entering the house, my head was dizzy, and a wave of irresistible heat rushed over me. I thought, maybe she was seriously injured, maybe she was lying in bed, maybe... different bad thoughts swirled around.

At night, I closed the windows as usual, tossing and turning in bed as usual. Suddenly, a thin girl, naked from the waist up, covered with stripes of blood, tears welling in her eyes, her mouth constantly sobbing, her face wearing a look of misery, appeared.

Finally, she cried, the corners of her mouth twitching, trembling in fear, as if she wanted to say something.

My mood was so disturbed that I couldn't sleep peacefully. I pushed open the window again, and the rain gently pattered. The distant lights flickered on and off as the leaves swayed. All around, everything was silent.

Drama 224

Timely Society

New New (780) 8:00 PM to 9:00 PM

"Slaughter"

"Slaughter" depicts a tragic event in the warlord civil war.

Aunt and sister-in-law and her nephew Xue'er, encountered A, B, and C, three soldiers in a deserted temple while fleeing. The three men killed each other to seize the stubborn woman. A stabbed B to death, and A was shot and killed by C. Xue'er was killed for helping his mother! As a result, when they were about to forcibly rape her, it became clear that the aunt and sister-in-law were his own sister and wife, and the Xue'er who was thrown to death was his own son! Although he later realized, it was too late!

News 225

The "Mimi Collection" monthly magazine published by the Yuanchang Advertising Company Broadcasting Station, No. 7, Sanxiafang, Caishi Road, Shanghai, has been well received by readers in various places. In order to reward the elegant intentions, various valuable gifts such as "round fans," "folding fans," "goldfish," "pairs," "zhongtang," and "silk fans" are prepared for gentlemen who purchase books widely. The gift method only requires purchasing over two dimes from the company to receive a pair of goldfish (with a fish storage bottle) as a gift, and more purchases will be rewarded with other gifts.

Movie News

Xinhua News 226

Ouyang Yuqian, director of the Xinhua Film Company, led Jin Yan, Hu Ping, Tong Yuejuan, Gu Menghu, and others to Hangzhou to film the outdoor scenes of "The Peach Blossom Fan." They have now all returned. After a test screening, the results are very satisfactory.

Hu Ping is grateful to Xie Sufang for being an actress who cross-dresses to play old dramas such as Hong Ni Guan. Her appearance is bright and beautiful, and her stage steps are solid. She is truly a rare talent.

Jin Yan likes to drink beer. Recently, as his work has become more intense, Jin Yan has been drinking more and more.

Before the premiere of "The Peach Blossom Fan," it is planned to carefully make a kind of round fan painted with peach blossoms, and a delicate sandalwood bone fan, to be widely gifted to all circles. It is currently being processed and printed.

Hollywood's Famous Playwright Visits "Triumphant Song" with Sassoon 227

Recently, a famous movie playwright from Hollywood, named Mackve, inquired about his friends in China about which production company was the greatest and wanted to visit it. So, his friends accompanied him to the Yihua Company. Coincidentally, Bu Wancang was directing "Triumphant Song." A magnificent set with a Chinese rural flavor stood in the studio. The actors Yuan Meiyun, Wang Yin, Yu Guilin, Qin Tong, Liu Guan Hongda, Jiang Xiu, and others were all dressed in summer clothes and acting. They found it very interesting and brought many "Ahmor" and "Rahm 克" cameras to take as many pictures as possible. Director Bu Cang introduced the actors to them. Mackve spoke English, saying that Miss Yuan was very lively and very "special blessing." They didn't leave until 12:30, and before leaving, they took a photo with all the staff.

A Play Within a Play in "The Song of One Heart" 228

"The Song of One Heart," Two Hearts in Waltz Time, starring the king of song, Carl Breilson, has completed the examination procedures in Nanjing and Shanghai and will be released in Shanghai soon. This is Breilson's latest and best work, with superior results far beyond "Bloodstains on the Song Robe" and "The Merry Emperor." There are three musical plays in the movie, depicting a group of women who, because they resent the false feelings of the men, escape to a deserted island and decide to sever relations with men. Later, the men chased after them in airplanes. At that time, the women on the island also felt that life was monotonous, and finally softened. Not only were the songs and music properly matched, but the performance also contained a satirical meaning. It is said that the fake airplane on the stage was completed by the set designer in only twelve hours when filming, but the appearance was no different from a real airplane, which can be said to be ingenious.

"Movie Star" Fitness Number Selling Well 229

"Movie Star Photo Collection" edited by Chen Jiazhen has been well received by movie fans since the first collection was published, and the sales have been unexpectedly good. The second collection is "Fitness Number," and the arrangement and material selection are even more outstanding. The whole book is printed in fine print on one hundred and twenty-pound copperplate paper. Each photo can be framed and placed on the desk, which is extremely beautiful. The book collects a book of fitness photos of more than thirty female stars, which is very rare. All major bookstores in the country sell it. If you want to try reading it, please attach a two-dime stamp and send it to Sanhe Publishing House, No. 54 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, and a copy will be sent immediately.
